## Analysis

The GT expression is:
$$0.877P\sin(0.567t) + 0.701(1 - P/65.75)P = -0.01066P^2 + 0.701P + 0.877P\sin(0.567t)$$

Expanding: $GT = -0.01066P^2 + 0.701P + 0.877P\sin(0.567t)$

This has the structure: $aP^2 + bP + cP\sin(dt)$

Now let me check candidates for this structure:

**Candidate 5**: $P^2 c_0 + P c_1 \sin(c_2 + c_3 t) + P c_4$

This equals $c_0 P^2 + c_4 P + c_1 P \sin(c_2 + c_3 t)$

Setting $c_0 = -0.01066$, $c_4 = 0.701$, $c_2 = 0$ (so $\sin(c_2 + c_3 t) = \sin(c_3 t)$), $c_3 = 0.567$, $c_1 = 0.877$.

Wait, but $\sin(0.567t) \neq \sin(c_2 + c_3 t)$ unless $c_2 = 0$. Actually, we can set $c_2 = -\pi/2$ to convert to cosine, but we need sine. Setting $c_2 = 0$ gives $\sin(c_3 t)$ which matches $\sin(0.567t)$.

This works! Ō£ō

**Candidate 4**: $P^2 c_0 + P c_1 + P c_2 \cos(c_3 t + c_4)$

Using $\cos(c_3 t + c_4) = \sin(c_3 t)$ when $c_4 = -\pi/2$:
Set $c_0 = -0.01066$, $c_1 = 0.701$, $c_2 = 0.877$, $c_3 = 0.567$, $c_4 = -\pi/2$.

This works! Ō£ō

**Candidate 6**: $P^2 c_0 + Pc_1 + Pc_2\sin(c_3 + c_4 t) + Pc_5$

Setting $c_0 = -0.01066$, $(c_1 + c_5) = 0.701$, $c_3 = 0$, $c_4 = 0.567$, $c_2 = 0.877$. Ō£ō

**Candidate 7**: Same idea with redundant $P^2$ terms. Ō£ō

**Candidate 8**: Similarly works. Ō£ō

Many other candidates also match by setting extra terms to zero. For example:
- **Candidates 18, 20, 21, 22, 25, 26, 39, 40, 64, 66, 68, 69, 73, 74** and others can all reduce to the GT form by appropriate parameter choices.

The most direct and clean matches are:

- **Candidate 4**: $P^2 c_0 + Pc_1 + Pc_2\cos(c_3 t + c_4)$ ŌĆö exact structural match using $\cos$ with phase shift $-\pi/2$.
- **Candidate 5**: $P^2 c_0 + Pc_1\sin(c_2 + c_3 t) + Pc_4$ ŌĆö exact structural match with $c_2 = 0$.
- **Candidate 6**: Same structure with extra $Pc_5$ term (redundant).
